Students in Shandong Stranded at Yanzhou Station 78

Jinan Correspondence: More than 1,000 students from seven schools including Tai'an No. 3 Middle School, County Normal School, Yanzhou No. 4 Rural Normal School, Three Vocational Schools, Qufu No. 2 Normal School, and Jining No. 7 Middle School, gathered in Yanzhou from the evening of the 16th, waiting for trains to go to Beijing to petition. As of this morning, it has been three days and nights, and the train has not yet departed. They are suffering from exposure and hunger. Many students are sick. Wang Yourong, the Yanzhou Traffic Division Chief of the Jinpu Railway, and the station personnel have been forced to flee. Railway telegrams and telephones are completely cut off. Southbound trains still arrive in Tai'an, and northbound trains still arrive in Tengxian. At 7:00 AM on the 18th, when the special train of Ma Hongkui, the commander-in-chief of the 15th Route Army, and Wang Shuhan, the representative of Zhang Xueliang, arrived in Yanzhou, the students stood on the tracks, not allowing the train to pass, asking Ma to negotiate with Han Fuqu, the chairman of the provincial government, on their behalf, to allocate vehicles and allow them to enter Beijing. Ma spoke with Han by long-distance telephone, and Han replied that he could find a way nearby in Yanzhou. Seeing that there was no solution, Ma ordered the students to board the confiscated No. 201 Pingpu train, and wait until his special train left the station before heading south. The students immediately boarded the train. Because there were few cars and many people, only half of them could fit. The rest planned to wait for the next train to Yanzhou before boarding. After Ma's special train left at 12:05 PM, the students' special train was still not allowed to depart. Four or five hundred northbound passengers in Yanzhou station were blocked at the station and could not go north, and cried out in distress. Gu Liangmin, the commander of the 22nd Division stationed in Yanzhou, telegraphed Han, asking for instructions. Han then ordered the Taishan armored train to go to Yanzhou at 10:30 PM last night to pick up the passengers to Jinan, but there was still no solution for the students' train. (19th)

Anhui Province, Wuyuan County, Captured by Bandits 79

▲ Representatives Sent from Shanghai to the Capital to Appeal

The Daily News reports that amidst the pressing foreign aggression and the confusion of national affairs, Zhu's Red Bandit troops from the Jiangxi border suddenly invaded Anhui Province, capturing Wuyuan County on the 17th. The Anhui Provincial Association in Shanghai, in order to rescue all the people of Anhui, yesterday specially sent representatives to Beijing to petition the Ministry of Military Affairs, requesting that troops be dispatched quickly to provide assistance. Their petition is as follows: "We have recently received a telegram from the Wuyuan Association in Shanghai stating that more than a thousand Red Bandits from the Jiangxi border have captured Wuyuan City, looting and killing rampantly, and the county magistrate has fled first. Upon hearing this news, the members of our association are extremely anxious. In addition to having already telegraphed your Ministry, begging you to order the troops stationed in Jiangxi and western Zhejiang to quickly suppress the bandits, we have now heard that Xiuning County in southern Anhui has also been captured. Considering that the Red Bandits are numerous and powerful, the people will have no survivors, and the disaster will inevitably spread throughout Anhui. Fearing that the previous telegram was not sufficient, we are now sending the standing committee members of our association, together with fellow villagers in Beijing, to deliver this letter and the original telegram, prostrating ourselves to plead for rescue on behalf of all the people of Wuyuan. We humbly request that you grant us an audience and promptly devise a plan to suppress the bandits and rescue the people, so as to secure the lives of the people and prevent the disaster from spreading throughout Anhui. This would be a great act of kindness. Respectfully submitted to He, Minister of the Ministry of Military Affairs."

According to the representatives who spoke to the Daily News reporter, Wuyuan County in Anhui Province is adjacent to the Jiangxi border. Several months ago, Zhu's bandits attempted to invade several times, but fortunately, the national army was able to block and suppress them, and the county was spared. Recently, all the troops stationed in the county have been transferred elsewhere, and there are no soldiers stationed in the county seat, which led to its capture by the Red Bandits on the morning of the 17th. After receiving the telegram, we immediately telegraphed Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, requesting that troops be sent nearby to provide assistance, but three days have passed and no reinforcements have arrived. If this continues day after day, the bandit forces will spread throughout Anhui, and Jiangsu and Zhejiang will also be at risk. The Anhui Provincial Association in Shanghai, in order to save the lives and property of the people of Anhui, has sent personnel to the provincial governments of Zhejiang, Anhui, and Jiangxi to petition for joint suppression, and has also sent the two of us to Beijing to petition the Ministry of Military Affairs. We also plan to convene fellow villagers in Beijing to discuss rescue measures.

Local Correspondence

Songjiang 80

Resignation and Replacements in County Party Headquarters: Zhu Tiexian and Huang Jikun, two executive members of the County Party Headquarters, have resigned from their positions due to other work, and their vacancies have remained unfilled for several months. Considering the heavy workload, the Provincial Executive Committee has ordered that Wu Jiaju and Wang Zhewu be appointed as formal executive members to fill the vacancies and attend the executive committee meetings with immediate effect.

Establishment of the National Salvation Conference Promotion Association: Chen Guisang, the principal of the local County Normal School, and others believe that, given the pressing foreign aggression, the people should jointly bear the responsibility for national survival. Recently, following Wang Jingwei's telegram, they initiated the National Salvation Conference, to be jointly participated by the people and the nation, to establish the foundation of democratic politics. A preparatory office for the Songjiang County Branch of the Jiangsu Promotion Association for the National Salvation Conference was organized and held a meeting at the People's Education Center this afternoon, electing responsible personnel to prepare and proceed.

Wuxi 81

Provincial Committee's Opinion on Party Affairs: Recently, some party members in the county organized a Party Affairs Reform Association, proposing to take over the County Party Headquarters. As a result, there have been conflicting rumors in society. Yang Xingquan and Zhang Gongren, two members of the Provincial Party Committee, came to Wuxi yesterday and convened a meeting at the County Party Headquarters with the local party, government, and police authorities, and also contacted representatives of the stationed troops. They emphasized that joint attention should be paid to local security and that all organizations in the county that lack legal basis should be strictly banned, as they confuse public opinion and affect local security. They also convened representatives from various districts and party headquarters, stating that all contributions that are beneficial to the party affairs of the county can be submitted to the higher-level party headquarters for review through legal procedures. The Party Affairs Reform Committee also held a meeting yesterday, sending a telegram in response to Mr. Wang Jingwei's telegram and issuing a declaration.

Murderer Sentenced to Death: Lu Deguan, a villager from Panshi near Zhangjingqiao in the seventh district of the county, was killed by bandits from the northeast during a bandit riot in the winter of the 16th year of the Republic of China, and his bones were buried to hide the evidence. The case remained unsolved. In March of this year, Zhu Meiji, the head of the security team in the eighth district, arrested three bandit suspects, Wang A'mei, Du Xiao'er, and Pan Fulang, and handed them over to the county, who were then transferred to the county court for trial and detention. Yesterday (the 19th) at around 6 p.m., Judge Huang ordered the police to bring the three criminals, Wang A'mei, and others, to court for trial, sentencing Wang A'mei to death and Du Xiao'er and Pan Fulang to twelve years of imprisonment each. After the sentencing, they were returned to custody.

Completion of Telephone Installation in the Four Townships: The County Construction Bureau, in order to facilitate communication between the city and the townships, previously drafted a plan to install telephones in the city and townships, prepared a budget, and submitted it to the Construction Department for approval. Currently, all eighteen urban and rural telephone stations have been completed on the 9th of this month, and test calls have been made. Director Yao submitted the telephone line map and a list of the remaining materials to the Construction Department yesterday for review and verification and requested that personnel be sent to Wuxi to inspect and accept the project before handing it over to the Wuxi exchange for management, so that calls can be made.

Changzhou 82

Student Union Decides Not to Resume Classes: The Wujin County Student Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association held an emergency representative meeting on the 19th to discuss how the association should respond to the current drastic changes in the situation regarding the issue of strikes. It was decided that classes would not resume until the government had provided a satisfactory response to the objectives of the strike.

Bandits Rampant Again in the Fourth District: The fourth district of Wujin County has always been a place where bandits roam. Now that it is winter, kidnapping bandits are rampant again. Xia Hanrong's family in Xiajiacun, Yingdong Township, in that district was robbed the night before, and Hanrong's son, Qifeng, was kidnapped. Zhang Hulin, who lives near the village, was also kidnapped on the same day. The Public Security Bureau has ordered that the bandits be arrested and brought to justice.

Zhenjiang 83

Announcement of Important Officials in Civil Affairs and Construction Departments: The newly appointed Director of the Construction Department, Dong Xiujia, was sworn in and assumed office the day before yesterday. Yesterday, the following important officials were announced: Chief Technician Chen Hefu, Secretaries Liu Baohe and Jiang Beicheng, First Section Chief Xu Ji, Second Section Chief Ying Jianzhou, Third Section Chief and Acting Fourth Section Chief Xu Tigang, Fifth Section Chief Liu Chunzhong, Sixth Section Chief Yu Liming, Technician Ge Hanlou, and Inspector Wu Pinjin. In addition, Qian Ciyan, the former First Section Chief of the Department of Civil Affairs, and Tao Mu, the former Second Section Chief, have resigned and gone elsewhere. The newly appointed Director Zhao Qilu announced yesterday that Wang Xizeng would be the Chief of the Second Section and acting Chief of the First Section. Furthermore, Zhang Peng, the Magistrate of Zhenjiang County, will be transferred to be the Secretary of the Department, and Mao Weixun, a local from Zhenjiang, will be the Chief of the Third Section, both of which have been internally decided.

General Student Demonstration Postponed: All students in Nantong County have gone on strike. The general demonstration, originally scheduled for the 19th at the public sports field, has been postponed to the 21st due to rain.

Huzhou 85

Bandits Rob and Injure the Victim: Shen A'bao, a farmer from Dingjiaqiao, Guannan Village, Qiao District, Wuxing County, Huzhou, who has some property, was suddenly visited by six or seven bandits at around 11 p.m. on the 16th of this month. They broke down the door with flashlights, knives, and clubs, and rummaged through boxes and cabinets, looting at will. All the cotton quilts, clothes, and other items were taken away. The victim, Shen A'bao, his son Xinglin, and his daughter-in-law were all beaten with wooden clubs by the bandits.

Letters Received

Letter from the Ministry of Railways 86

Dear Sir, Upon reading the special telegram in your newspaper, it stated that Minister Lian of our ministry had requested to resign from the National Government but was not approved, and on the 16th, he requested a ten-day leave from the Executive Yuan and left Beijing for Shanghai immediately, with Chen Yanjiong temporarily acting on his behalf. According to the facts, this is completely untrue. Minister Lian, due to the recurrence of an old illness, requested and was granted leave by the Executive Yuan for recuperation starting on the 5th of this month, and the National Government was notified for record. During the leave period, Deputy Minister Qian Zongze was acting on his behalf. Later, due to his prolonged illness, he requested to resign and was instructed by the Executive Yuan to stay and was granted an additional eleven days of leave for medical treatment. Minister Lian was originally scheduled to return to Beijing from Shanghai on the 16th of this month. We hope your newspaper will publish this letter to clarify the truth. Sincerely, Ministry of Railways, December 18th.

President of Jiangsu Provincial Middle School Requests Education Director Cheng Tianfang to Take Office 87

▲Visiting Chairman Gu in Zhenjiang Together

(Zhenjiang Correspondence) Cheng Tianfang, the new member of the Jiangsu Provincial Committee and Education Director, has submitted a request to the Central Government to resign from the position in the Education Department. It is reported that the purpose of this unexpected visit was (1) to express welcome to Chairman Gu, (2) to urge Director Cheng to take office in the province as soon as possible, (3) to request the provincial government to order the payment of school expenses for October from the revenue collected during the peak harvest season as soon as possible, and (4) to continue to allocate the 300,000 yuan of education funds from the Shada revenue of the Financial Department and the 300,000 yuan of subsidies from the provincial government. Chaoyang College Adds Frontier Politics Courses 88

The Ministry of Education received a report from Chaoyang College, a private institution, stating that the college originally had a Faculty of Law with three departments: Law, Politics, and Economics, which had been reported to the Ministry. However, it has recently observed that China's borders are vast and sparsely populated, and many resources have not been developed. It is a pity to abandon resources on the ground, and the close proximity of strong neighbors creates constant coveting. The lack of effective border management is also a cause for concern. In addition, in recent years, water and drought disasters have spread throughout the inland, and people facing famine have no way to make a living. In order to alleviate the people's livelihood, it is essential to follow Dr. Sun Yat-sen's industrial plan and promote immigration to the Northeast Provinces, Mongolia, Xinjiang, Qinghai, and Tibet. However, managing border affairs requires specialized talents. Otherwise, without proper management, it will not only be a vain attempt to develop the borders but also lead to the contempt of foreign powers. Recognizing this, and in accordance with the National Government's emphasis on practical disciplines, the college has added a Department of Frontier Politics under the Faculty of Commerce this year to cultivate specialized talents to serve the country. Enrollment has begun this year, with eligibility limited to graduates of senior high schools. The study period is four years, and the subjects for the entrance examination are the same as those for other departments in the Faculty of Commerce. Forty students have been admitted and one class has been established, starting classes in September of this year. In addition to submitting a list of students admitted to the Department of Frontier Politics for review and record, all the reasons for the establishment of the Department of Frontier Politics under the Faculty of Commerce are hereby submitted for review. The Ministry of Education instructed that, given that the college originally had departments of Politics and Economics, courses related to frontier politics should be added to the final year of those two departments, and there is no need to establish a separate Department of Frontier Politics. The students admitted to the department this semester can be transferred to the departments of Politics and Economics.

Local News

Jing Hengyi Discusses the Foundation of National Education 89

After arriving in Shanghai from Guangdong, Jing Hengyi, a member of the Central Committee, returned to his ancestral home in Luyi Township before heading to Beijing by night train last night. When interviewed by a reporter from this newspaper at his friend's residence, Jing Hengyi stated that his joining the Kuomintang was based on the advocacy of National Foundation Education. During the Fifth Plenary Session of the Second National Congress in the 17th year of the Republic, he proposed reforming the salt administration and designating all salt revenue to fund National Foundation Education. The government at that time had no way to implement it, so it was not realized. This time, he entered Beijing with the same intention. If National Foundation Education cannot be implemented after the unified government is established, the Kuomintang will be completely disappointed. When the reporter asked about the content of the National Foundation Education proposal, he said: (1) Designate all salt revenue to fund this education, limited to compulsory education for so-called minors and continuing education and popular education for adults; (2) Establish a National Foundation Education institution directly under the National Government; (3) The salt administration agency is directly under the National Government, called the National Government Salt Tax Institute; (4) Organize a Salt Administration Reform Committee, hiring specialized personnel as members, and education administrators should also participate; (5) Education administration agencies may send personnel to supervise at any time and any place; (6) To adjust the revenue of the Ministry of Finance, a gradual reduction method should be used annually, and after five years, the salt tax will be completely unrelated to the Ministry of Finance; (7) For foreign debt relations, before the unequal treaties are abolished, a certain year can be used as a reference.

Jinan Defeats Shanghai Team in Final Three Minutes 101

▲A Score of Three to Two ▲A Scene from the Group A Match

Jinan football team, to pass safely through the terrifying waves, and to overcome the Shanghai team in the last three minutes, is it not difficult and gratifying? The score was three to two, which was a scene from the Group A match. Six thousand spectators in Yiyuan were surprised and delighted.

▲Jinan Revenge

It may not be possible to take great revenge in case of emergency. However, the situation was very bad yesterday, and there were many dangers. The new goalkeeper Chen Buzhang saved many goals and is worthy of praise. The other players were just average.

▲Fisherman's Gain

For the first fifteen minutes, neither side won. Although Jinan attacked from time to time, they did not shoot accurately. Then a shocking news came, Jinan suddenly lost a point. Jiang Shan Jing saw that things had gone wrong and also went to rescue him along the same road. Bai Kesi De shot to the left. Jinber rushed up, fiercely and unstoppably. The ball hit someone and can be said that the fisherman reaped the benefits.

Jinan did not show weakness. Chen Zhenhe shot fiercely in front of the goal, hitting the goal. Carnall was able to save it. The Shanghai team also attacked. Bai Kesi De and Jinber were in danger. Chen Buzhang wanted to save it and fell to the ground. Fortunately, Feng Yunyou headed it out when it was thirty minutes. Chen, Qiu, and Luo went up side by side, about to reach the goal. Fa Ping hooked it out. Mei threw it in. Luo, then Chen, then Qiu. Qiu shot. Ka was not allowed to come out. Long ran in to kick someone, slipped and fell to the ground. Everyone sighed. Chen Zhenhe took advantage of the situation to挑, passing over Ka's head and falling into the goal. Ka turned to the goal, and the ball had crossed the white line.

▲Second Tie

Everyone was delighted. Soon, Jinan scored again. Mei Hongbao advanced from the right and turned to the left. Chen Zhenhe got it. Seeing that it was full of enemies, he quickly passed it to Qiu. Dongyan lightly拨, rolling in. In the first half, Jinan took the lead with two to one. At the beginning of the second half, the Shanghai team pressed the goal. Chen Buzhang rushed out. Donghua Defeats Lehua in Senior Cup Replay 103

▲Result: Four to Zero

丨Tense First Half, Bland Second Half丨

Donghua and Lehua, who had previously fought to a draw in the Senior Cup, replayed for ninety minutes at the Zhonghua Baseball Field yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM. Under the whistle of referee Jiang Xiangqing, Donghua defeated Lehua with four to zero, winning the Senior Cup semi-final qualification.

▲Donghua Team

Zhou Xianyan Li Ning Guan Xuanan Chen Pu Tu Kaiyuan Chen Jiaqiu

Qian Jingyong Li Yichen Dai Linjing Chen Hongguang Chen Yutian

▲Lehua Team

Lu Zhongen Lu Zhiming Zhao Xiasheng Gu Shangdong Wang Shusen Chen Chao

Sun Huipei Wan Xianghua Jiang Chao Zhou Shaowen Li Lin

▲Wonderful Start

The muddy field showed the initial exhibition of war clouds, and the waves were astonishing. The east and west corresponded to each other, which was extremely wonderful and worth seeing. Lehua took the lead and sent the ball over, and the internal defender went forward in five directions to take advantage of the gap. The interior was empty and precarious. A strong wind suddenly came to the rescue, and the ball was blown back in the middle. Zhou Juewen could not stop his foot, and finally relieved the siege with an offside. Donghua took advantage of this to counterattack and went all the way. The goalkeeper Lu personally went outside the pass to resist the various forces and was calculated by others. Lehua's Li Lin挑ed in from the right, and Wan Xianghua headed the ball, but was surrounded and caught. Donghua raised a large army again. Xie Kaiyuan took advantage of the corner kick to shoot with the trend, and Lu Yaoqi caught it. One can be called a quick eye, and the other a quick foot. Lehua's Wan Xianghua performed wonderfully and became an instant hit. In the enemy's formation, he went in and out freely. If he had good assistants, he should be recorded in the book of merit.

Donghua Scores Three Goals in a Row 104

For twenty minutes, no one was in danger of being overthrown in the evil waves. This was because the forward was sharp and the inside was stable and strong. Huadong's Li Yichen opened the record, and the ball shot from the flat ground, as fast as an arrow. Lu could do nothing about it. Fifteen minutes later, the center defender Tu Kaiyuan挑ed in from the right, falling into the upper left corner of the goal. Lu tried to hit it, but the enemy rushed to the ball in the midst of confusion and it bounced into the total nest. Donghua won the second goal. Five minutes later, Chen Hongguang and Dai Linjing kicked twice in succession, both hitting Lu's body. Lehua's Chen Chao came to the rescue, but he made a fool of himself and打入 himself. Lehua lost another goal, losing three goals, which stirred up the morale of the army. The whole army rushed forward, and Zhou Xianyan became the target of the public. At that time, he was lucky to be safe. At the end of the first half, Donghua took the lead with three to zero.

The Situation in the Second Half Was Bland 105

In the second half, Lehua turned to take the upper hand and should have done something. However, it was unexpectedly lackluster. Perhaps the spirit was lost and the morale of the army was scattered. However, the internal defense was important and worked hard to resist, and the enemy was not easy to underestimate. It was true. The forward's attack on the city was only occasional. At the beginning, he saw Ronghua being invaded, one attack and one defense, for a long time. At thirty minutes, he once sent troops outside the pass. Jiang Chao仰攻 from the right and was rescued by Zhou. From then on, he stayed in the pass to carry out defense work. At thirty-seven minutes, Chen Hongguang was twenty yards in front of the goal. When he was seemingly not advancing, he suddenly raised his foot and swept out. The goalkeeper was startled, and the ball had entered the goal. After Lehua's defeat, he suddenly had the heart to retaliate. The crowd was united and the momentum was strong and difficult to suppress. For a time, the Donghua goal was in a panic again. If it were not for Zhou's composure and Li Guan's courage, it would be difficult to relieve the siege. When the break whistle sounded, Donghua returned in triumph with four to zero.

In addition, sixteen important attendants and three servants also went to Beijing by train.

▲Talks by Qin Zhen When the members were boarding the train, a reporter from Xin Sheng She specially visited Mr. Qin Liming on the train. He was given the opportunity to give a speech, saying that in today's situation in our country, internal and external troubles are coming together. In terms of internal affairs, after the flood, how to save the victims and plan the post-disaster construction, and how to realize democratic politics and determine the permanent foundation of the country in politics, are all the most urgent tasks at present. However, due to time constraints, I cannot talk about it in detail. Now I will abandon these two questions and first talk about the most urgent diplomatic problem. In terms of my personal opinions, the attitude and preparation that the people of the country should urgently adopt now, since the Japanese occupied Liaoji, the whole country has been aroused by patriotic enthusiasm and has launched anti-Japanese and national salvation movements, organized volunteer armies, and organized aid-Ma groups, etc. The enthusiastic feelings of striving for survival for the motherland and the nation are indeed worthy of admiration by the world. At the same time, students have risen up to petition the government, demanding a declaration of war against Japan. Their intentions are indeed commendable, but their actions are too superficial. It must be known that today's methods for us to deal with Japan, on the one hand, we should make a painful determination, and on the other hand, we should use a calm spirit to make a vow to fight to the death, so that we can gain more practical benefits in fact, and unnecessary sacrifices can also be reduced. Therefore, my personal opinion is that we should not declare war against Japan now, but should quickly change the declaration of war to the preparation for war. Since we are talking about war, we should first study how we can fight. If we fight with others, how is the training of our army? How is the equipment and food for combat? How is the finance for combat? Even the people of the country should examine their physical fitness and see whether they have the ability to resist the enemy for a long time when they meet in battle. None of these should be carefully analyzed and prepared. Moreover, the timing of the war is not fixed. We must ask ourselves whether we have the preparation for a long-term war before we can talk about war. Let's take another look at Germany during the European War. After years of preparation and planning, the result was that it was food shortages that were the biggest cause of failure. Today, Japan has been planning against us for more than a day. In the past, it has long-term reserves for pre-war preparations, whether it is equipment or food. However, we want to use an unprepared country to deal with a prepared country. The situation is really impossible. Therefore, in the future, our country should adopt proper defense and quickly work hard to prepare itself, so that the methods of war can圖 the survival of the nation and win the final victory.

▲Talks by Jing Hengyi Central Committee member Jing Tingyi, after arriving in Shanghai from his hometown Shangyu yesterday morning, took a train to Beijing that night. A reporter from Xin Sheng She met Mr. Jing yesterday and asked him for his opinions on the political situation. According to Mr. Jing, I joined the Kuomintang specifically to promote national education as my main proposition. At the Fifth Plenary Session of the Second Congress seventeen years ago, I had a proposal to reform the entire salt administration revenue and筹办 national education. The government at the time had no way to implement it, meaning that the people would not be educated, so how could there be a movement. This time I went to Beijing with the same purpose, and said that if national education cannot be办 again after the establishment of the unified government, then the Kuomintang will be completely disappointed.

▲Members Going to Beijing in the Afternoon The Central Committee members who took the Beijing-Shanghai night express train to Beijing last night included Xiong Kewu, Xu Chongzhi, Jing Hengyi, Chen Bijun, and He Yaozu. ▲Important Statement For the statement, since the disturbance of the Chamber of Commerce's affairs occurred, the Chamber of Commerce has issued an announcement expressing its solemn attitude. It is heard that recently, some people have falsely borrowed the name of the Chamber of Commerce and gone to various trade associations to冒盖 seals, and claimed that because the Chamber of Commerce cannot hold meetings, they will convene meetings elsewhere, etc., which is deeply hated. The Chamber of Commerce will convene a general meeting of members in accordance with the provisions of the Chamber of Commerce Law, with its proper procedures and its proper meeting place, and it must also be announced in the newspaper, otherwise it is falsely borrowing the name and using it for other purposes. ▲Chairman's Speech Wang Xiaolai, the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, gave a speech yesterday, saying that regarding the fact that the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce was allegedly led by the so-called Shanghai Special Municipal Merchant Sports Committee to receive it by violence with plainclothes徒众, I have solemnly expressed my attitude. The Businessmen's Movement Committee of this city, under the premise that the takeover of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has not yet been realized, began its work in the Industrial Bank building on Jiujiang Road. The news from yesterday is recorded below. A reporter from Datong News Agency made a special visit to Mr. Feng at his private residence yesterday, inquiring about the organizational significance of the Businessmen's Movement Committee, its process, and what measures it would take in the future. Shi Zhikun was also present. The two gentlemen jointly issued the following responsible statement. Mr. Feng said, "I appreciate the inquiries from your reporter. The fragmentary records are insufficient to explain the essential principles upheld by our colleagues and cannot dispel the doubts and concerns of the Shanghai business community. Therefore, we have compiled a simple statement for public release, which I believe your reporter will agree with. We firmly believe that China's current situation requires first addressing external threats to secure internal stability. Only through the united efforts of the entire nation to save the country can the Manchurian problem be resolved satisfactorily. Based on this key principle, the Shanghai Businessmen's Movement Committee was organized to promote the Shanghai business movement under the guidance of the leaders of the Nationalist Party and to achieve the following objectives: (1) Return civil rights to the people. In other words, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce is an organization of the people, and its rights should be immediately returned to the business community of Shanghai. (2) Abolish all special laws and protect all freedoms of the people. For the past four years, we have suffered immensely from dictatorship and autocracy. The nation is on the verge of collapse, and our people must rise up and seek solutions themselves. We must recognize that without the protection of all freedoms and the ability to exercise all rights, the people will be powerless and defenseless, only fit to be slaves of a conquered nation. They cannot serve as the foundation for building a stable country, nor can they resist the violent invasion of Japan. (3) Punish those responsible for the Liaoning Incident. History shows that there are ministers who lose their country, but never people who lose their country. However, after a country is lost, it is the people who suffer the most. For the sake of restoring discipline and saving the country from danger, how can we not punish the officials who have failed in their duties to demonstrate national credibility and unite the people's will? Only in this way can we deter traitors and rigorously investigate responsibilities to establish a grand plan for a century of stability. Based on these three points, we will never falter. Therefore, there was the previous attempt to take over the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. Taking over the Municipal Chamber of Commerce from a group of party traitors and returning the General Chamber of Commerce to the business community of the entire city is the first step in realizing civil rights. No one who willingly serves as a lackey to the party traitors would disagree with this. We are all citizens of the Republic of China, and we should not be so confused as to be willing to be puppets of the party traitors and be manipulated by them. However, at this critical time of national crisis, all our actions must be taken with utmost caution. If there is the slightest resemblance to the actions of the party headquarters on April 18th of the past eighteen years, we must be vigilant. The only thing we hope for at present is that the people can exercise their freedom of will and restore their past power, then our mission will be complete. If, in the meantime, unfortunate events occur in Shanghai, seeking peace but finding danger, seeking benefit but finding harm, it would be detrimental to the merchants. However, if the merchants are willing to be puppets of the party traitors and protect them, then the public anger of the entire city's merchants has been building for a long time, and the will of the people has been violated. A positive conflict may be unavoidable. This is what I am reluctant to say, but it is not the fault of our colleagues, but the evil consequences of the manipulation of the party members and the exposure of the incompetence of the merchants. Using this to confront foreign aggression is not enough to overcome the stubborn invasion of Japan. Using this to confront domestic issues is not enough to establish national peace and stability. At that time, we can only plead guilty to the people of the future and will never shamelessly associate with the party traitors. The Businessmen's Movement Committee has not been public for long, and we fear that outsiders may not be clear about it, so we have summarized its essentials to present to the business community of the entire city. What to do and where to go is their own choice." (Signed by Feng Shaoshan and Shi Zhikun)

Tragedy at the Wing On Textile Factory in Wusong 120

▲Major Clash Between Workers and Police

▲More Than a Hundred Shots Fired

▲Several Workers Wounded

Yesterday, a clash occurred at the Wing On Textile Factory on Yunzao Road in Wusong due to a worker slowdown. It involved the police detachment dispatched by the Municipal Public Security Bureau. Over a hundred shots were fired, wounding several workers, and order was disrupted. The authorities declared a special state of martial law. The details are listed as follows:

▲Cause of the Incident According to reports, the old and new Wing On factories employ a total of over six thousand male and female workers. The origin of this disturbance was the workers' demand that the factory pay four months' worth of bonuses. Negotiations with Mr. Guo Shun, the general manager of the factory, failed to reach a satisfactory conclusion. As a result, there was a general slowdown on the afternoon of the day before yesterday. At that time, a small part of the machinery in the new factory was vandalized. Yesterday, the factory, due to unresolved conditions, was deeply concerned that the workers would cause further disturbances. For safety reasons, the factory locked all the machine rooms and announced a shutdown. The Municipal Public Security Bureau police detachment dispatched Squad Leader Gu, leading more than thirty armed police officers, to protect the factory. Yesterday, at about 5:00 PM, male and female workers continued to arrive at the factory to work. Seeing that the gate was tightly closed, they could not enter. They also saw a large number of police officers guarding outside the gate. Before long, a conflict occurred, and the tragedy began.

▲Details of the Conflict When the situation became tense, a reporter rushed to investigate. At that time, the reporter saw that the factory gate was tightly closed, and thousands of male and female workers were gathered outside the factory, standing on the side of the road. Soon, a team of people, holding small red flags, gave speeches to the workers. At about 6:00 PM, the crowd tried to enter the gate, and the police officers guarding the gate fired four or five shots and retreated westward. Seeing this, Zeng, the director of the Seventh District of the Public Security Bureau, came out of the factory and reported to the Municipal Public Security Bureau by long-distance telephone. The crowd then attacked and opened the gate and poured into the factory. The reporter was also squeezed into the crowd. Soon, the crowd destroyed the office and staff dormitories. At this time, the police officers had sneaked into the interior of the factory from the side door on the west side. They met the crowd, and seeing that the situation was not good, they fired about a hundred shots to demonstrate to the crowd. At this point, the crowd began to retreat outwards. Order was disrupted for a time, and the reporter had retreated from the side door to avoid it temporarily. Wang Yucheng, a standing member of the Eighth District Party Department, also weaved through the crowd to avoid it. Zhao Ze Zhou, the director of the Seventh District of the Public Security Bureau, and Zeng Keguang, the director of the office, discussed reporting to the First Regiment of the Seventy-Eighth Division of the garrison and requesting that troops be sent to suppress it.

▲Injury Investigation After the incident, an investigation found that those injured by stray bullets had been sent to Wusong Haibin Public Hospital. They included male worker Li Lunyin, 23 years old, whose neck was pierced by a bullet, bleeding heavily; Gu Jinxiang, 20 years old, a local, who was shot in the left arm; and female worker Jiao Lianying, age unknown, whose skull was fractured. According to Jiang Yisheng, the director of the hospital, Jiao Lianying was beyond rescue, Li Lunyin was also in critical condition, and Gu Jinxiang was not in serious condition. Police officer Wang Heting was injured in the head by a stone. There were several other minor injuries. After the doctors bandaged them, they were discharged from the hospital.

▲Declaration of Martial Law After the incident, the garrison, fearing that rioters would take the opportunity to cause trouble, declared a special state of martial law. All major roads were closed to pedestrians to maintain peace in the city of Wusong. At about 10:00 PM, the reporter accompanied Zhao, the director of the Seventh District of the Public Security Bureau, Zeng, the director of the office, Wang Yucheng, a standing member of the Party Department, and Zhao, the deputy officer of the garrison, to inspect the factory. They saw that the room was full of messes, appliances, and objects were destroyed, and the loss was estimated at tens of thousands of dollars or more. Therefore, it was impossible to start work for a while.

Record of the Meeting of the Pharmaceutical Workers' Union 121

The Shanghai Pharmaceutical Workers' Union held its city-wide representative assembly yesterday. More than 1,000 people attended. The presidium included Zhao Zhenhui, Fang Qinghe, Chen Hezhi, Xu Zhibao, Zhou Wenhao, and Zhou Dichuchen as the recorder. Lin Meiyan, a city representative, performed the rituals. Chairman Zhao Zhenhui reported on the situation on the 18th when Chen Xuetang and Fang Zheng led unemployed vagrants to break into the office. Fang Qinghe expressed his opinion that he was not aware of the unfortunate incident on the 18th. He received a notice from the association on that day to attend an emergency meeting. The association stated that it should not come to take over without the approval of the general membership meeting. The current directors and supervisors were all produced by the general membership meeting and entrusted by the crowd. How can they transfer without the permission of all members? How can they face the crowd? If approved by the general membership meeting, he will proceed with the transfer procedures. The guidance of the superior representative Lin Meiyan (omitted). The discussion then began: (A) Is the association willing to be reorganized by Fang Zheng, etc.? Please make a public decision. Resolution: (1) Before legal procedures are completed, the association cannot recognize anyone who comes to take over. If it comes to take over after legal procedures, it must also be approved by the general membership meeting before it can be transferred. (2) Fang Zheng, etc., came to take over without legal procedures and instructed unemployed vagrants such as Qi Jinxian, Chen Xuetang, and Li Baokang to destroy the office. An application should be submitted to the higher authorities for arrest. (B) The illegal reorganization committee's publication in Shen Xin's two newspapers said that the association's finances falsely reported accounts and all went into private pockets, which inevitably made members suspicious. Representatives should be elected by the members to review all the accounts of the association to see if there is any case of fraud. It was resolved that representatives should be elected by members of each district to review, starting on the 25th. After the review, they will be responsible for public announcement. (C) What should be done with the 448 copies of blank association certificates that were robbed from the association? Resolution: Members in each industry should pay attention to whether there are any non-members in the shops who have obtained certificates recently. If so, they should report it to the association immediately for investigation. (D) Membership fees and stamps for this month have already been issued. Should they continue to be collected? Resolution: The officers of each district should be responsible for continuing to collect and issue a notice to all members, prohibiting them from delaying payment. If anyone falsely uses other names to collect monthly fees, members should arrest them and hand them over to the local military police organs or the patrol room and report to the association for handling.

A Large Number of Overseas Chinese from Mexico Will Return to China 125

▲Transported by Gypsum Ship

The China Press reported that the shipping industry in this port received news from San Francisco on Saturday and Sunday that a specially chartered cargo ship carrying gypsum will soon arrive in Shanghai with 300 Chinese refugees from Mexico. These people were expelled due to the anti-Chinese movement in Mexico and are now scattered in San Francisco and the western coast ports of Mexico. They are all destitute. The expenses will be provided by the Chinese Consul General in San Francisco. It was originally planned to transport them in batches on ships transporting wheat from the United States to China. However, due to the fact that the refugees living in various seaports in Mexico cannot enter the United States to board the ships, it would be too expensive and difficult to send a special wheat transport ship to various seaports in Mexico to transport them. At that time, Mexico had a large amount of gypsum for sale to China. The Chinese Consul General in San Francisco negotiated with Mr. Comeyn, who was responsible for transporting wheat, to rent a ship. In addition to transporting gypsum to Mexico, it also recruited Chinese refugees at various ports in Mexico to board the ship. Finally, it departed from San Francisco and came to Shanghai. These refugees are almost all Cantonese. Therefore, after the ship arrives in Shanghai and unloads the gypsum, it will sail to Guangzhou. The number of people may be more than 300.

Liu Da Jun Returned Home the Day Before Yesterday 126

Mr. Liu Dajun, Director of the National Government's Bureau of Statistics, has returned home after more than four months of representing our country at international statistical conferences. He arrived at the Gonghexiang Wharf at 9:00 AM on the 19th. Those who welcomed him at the port included representatives from the Bureau of Statistics, China Critic Weekly, Chinese Economic Society, Research Committee, and Liu's family members, totaling dozens of people. During his trip, Mr. Liu attended the International Statistical Conference, the International Population Conference, and the International Economic Design Conference. He also inspected the statistical systems and economic conditions of various European countries, and he gained a lot of experience. It is said that he will write articles and publish them successively in the near future.

Opening of the Nan Shi Shelter for the Needy 127

▲ Opens on the 15th of this month

▲ The number of people has reached over a thousand

Every winter, the Shanghai Charity Organizations United Association sets up temporary shelters for the needy in Nanshi and Zhabei to accommodate the poor. Now that it is deep winter, these shelters are being set up again following past practice. The first shelter is located at the Chaozhou Guild Hall on Chezhan Road in Nanshi, and the second is located at the Chao Hui Villa on Longhua Road. If these are not enough, other houses will be found for expansion. In the past, the shelters have only accommodated men, not women. This year, a women's shelter will also be added to avoid disappointment, and a suitable house is currently being sought. In Zhabei, there is already a disaster relief shelter, and it is planned to open a shelter as soon as the disaster relief efforts are completed. The two shelters in Nanshi opened on the 15th of this month, and within a few days, the number of people accommodated has reached over a thousand. This is because there are more poor people this year due to the disaster. However, the shelters have no dedicated funding, relying on subsidies from various charities and temporary fundraising. This year, various charities and local gentry and merchants have repeatedly donated to disaster relief efforts in various provinces, making fundraising for the shelters particularly difficult.

▲ The third batch of over eight thousand seven hundred yuan has been remitted

The County Public Funds Office Requests Exemption of the Two-Yuan Surtax on Grain 130

Yesterday, Jiang Shijie and Kang Yongnian, directors of the Shanghai County Public Funds and Public Property Management Office, telegraphed the National Government, the Ministry of Finance, the Jiangsu Provincial Government, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance, and the Shanghai County Government, stating that due to the famine and hardship, it was imperative to exempt farmers from the two-yuan surtax on grain to provide relief. The draft reads: "Concerning the urgent matter of the famine and hardship, we implore you to promptly exempt the two-yuan surtax on grain to uphold the integrity of the government and comfort the people. According to the records, Qin Xitian, the former director of our office, and others submitted a petition in the 19th year of the Republic stating that the two-yuan surtax per shi (unit of dry measure) of grain should not be a permanent practice and requested that your ministry and the Ministry of Finance establish a separate tax law. The Ministry of Finance approved this with document number 11557, stating, 'Upon investigation, this case has been approved to be temporarily limited to the winter grain of the 19th year only and must not be increased again.' The ministry's order is clear and should be eternally followed. However, this year, Jiangsu Province is levying a winter grain tax that still includes a one-yuan surtax per shi, disregarding the people's hardship and failing to consider the political system. After deliberation by the district chiefs and accountants of our county, it was decided that we should urgently request your ministry to order the Ministry of Finance to comply with the approved document, cease the two-yuan surtax, and uphold your ministry's prestige. Furthermore, this year, the excessive rains have caused a disaster, reducing the autumn harvest. The Jiangsu Provincial Government has already verified the disaster and reduced the tax accordingly. We request that you clearly announce whether our county has already reduced or discounted the tax to dispel public doubts. This is our special request for your consideration, as it is a matter of public concern."

Fellow Townsmen from Wuyuan and Huining Request Troops to Suppress Bandits 131

The Shanghai Wuyuan Fellow Townsmen Association received news that the county seat had been attacked and looted by bandits. The Huining Fellow Townsmen Association in Shanghai, due to the attack on Wuyuan by Jiangxi bandits, the looting of the entire city, the jailbreak from the county office, and the public panic, sent telegrams to the governments of Anhui and Zhejiang provinces, urgently requesting that nearby garrisons be dispatched to suppress the bandits day and night to prevent them from fleeing elsewhere. The Yixian Fellow Townsmen Association Receives News of a Police Mutiny 132

The Yixian Fellow Townsmen Association in Shanghai received an urgent letter from their hometown yesterday, stating that the county police force of over thirty men suddenly mutinied at noon on the 10th of this month. Led by patrol chief Wang Derong, they surrounded the county government in the name of demanding pay, kidnapped Secretary Huang and Yu Zhicheng, the head of the finance bureau, and gentry members such as Hu Yuanji. They fired shots as a show of force and extorted a large sum of money, causing chaos and panic throughout the city. Fortunately, a portion of the police force that did not mutiny, led by Captain Ding, tracked and pursued the mutineers, who then dispersed and fled towards the Qibian area in the fourth and fifth districts. It is reported that more than ten guns were recovered, but seven rifles are still missing. The losses to merchants and residents are estimated to be around three thousand yuan.

▲ More than ten thousand visitors attended

Local News 2

Another Proposal to Stop New Year's Greetings 135

Lin Youren and others advocated stopping New Year's greetings to commemorate the national crisis, as reported in previous newspapers. Recently, Ma Gongyu and Ma Mengrong of Great China University sent letters to various organizations, suggesting reforming empty formalities, stating: "As the New Year approaches, people from all walks of life will, as usual, exchange greeting cards, 'Wishing a Happy New Year.' Although this is a meaningless formality, it can be tolerated in peaceful times. However, with the Northeast fallen, the Southwest in alarm, the nation in imminent danger, and the people struggling to survive, there is no time for condolences, let alone celebrations. Empty formalities should be abolished with determination, and patriotism should be more than just empty talk. Sending New Year's cards seems like a minor matter, but when considered on a national scale, it has significant implications. Assuming that each person spends two yuan on purchasing cards and postage, and if this activity is engaged in by just one percent of the national population, the total cost would be eight million yuan. Over ten years, this amounts to eighty million yuan. Such a huge sum, if used for any beneficial cause for the country, would be far better than the meaningless formality of 'wishing a happy New Year.' Moreover, the fashionable greeting cards sold in the market are either directly imported from foreign countries or printed with foreign paper materials, with none entirely made of domestic materials. Young men and women, in addition to wearing foreign clothes, watching foreign movies, and using foreign fountain pens, still feel they have not fully realized their ability to Europeanize. Therefore, they must compete and vie with each other in greeting cards, imitating Westerners. The poverty of the country and the hardship of the people are not their concern. Patriotic compatriots, who usually shout slogans to 'Overthrow Imperialism,' will donate millions of yuan every New Year for this meaningless formality, to pay homage to the imperialists, helping their strength to invade us. Is this not regrettable? Therefore, this kind of 'Wishing a Happy New Year' can be rightly called 'Wishing the Imperialists a Happy New Year,' which is not an exaggeration." It can be seen that "stopping New Year's greetings" has become the consensus of the people.

Thug Attempts to Evade Responsibility for Extortion 139

▲ Claims he was only following to observe the situation

▲ Detective Tang recounts the capture

Li Jinzhi from Tongzhou wrote threatening letters between the 12th of last month and the 7th of this month, extorting 1,000 yuan and 500 taels of silver from Wang Long, a Ningbo native and owner of the Wang Longji Laundry Company at No. 2534 Zhoujiashui Road. After the case was uncovered, Tang Jian, a Chinese detective from the General Inspectorate, and Wu Changkai, a detective, arrested him and brought him to the First Special District Court for questioning. He denied the charges and was detained for investigation. Yesterday, Judge Shen Bingrong continued the hearing in a higher court. Zhang Tianyin, the detective's lawyer, stated that his accomplices could not be arrested during the period of rescheduling. The victim, Wang Long, testified that he saw the defendant and two others in front of the Dasheng Temple in Hongzhen, Zhabei. The defendant lingered on the road three or four times, then stepped forward and asked him if he was the Wang from Zhoujiashui Road. Wang replied in the affirmative. Just as they were about to continue talking, the detectives arrived and arrested the defendant. The other two thugs were standing far away, one tall and one short. When questioned, the defendant firmly denied any involvement, claiming that the plaintiff's statements were entirely fabricated and that the incident was committed by his friend, Ji Shan, who was at large. He claimed that he saw their suspicious behavior, so he followed them to observe the situation and intended to report any minor matters to the detective. The court ordered him to write the key phrases and numbers from the threatening letter on the spot for handwriting comparison. After examining the handwriting, the court declared to him, "You are a worker at the Meifu Electric Light Factory, not a detective's partner, and it is absurd for you to make such a claim of tailing someone to gain merit." The defendant also stated that if he had spoken to the plaintiff, he would be willing to accept severe punishment. Zhang, the detective's lawyer, stated that Detective Tang witnessed the incident and requested his testimony. According to Tang Jian's testimony, he saw the defendant and the two others walking out of the Dasheng Temple and lingering. As soon as they saw the plaintiff's sign of a Pu Bao towel, they approached him. Seeing that the area was remote, he feared that the plaintiff would be harmed, so he went forward. The defendant then fled, but was eventually captured. Judge Shen then ordered Li Jinzhi to be remanded in custody pending a scheduled sentencing.

Sichuan Woman Sues for Fraudulent Marriage 141

▲ Dismissed by the court

Zhang Yang Xianfen, a woman from Baxian County, Sichuan Province, is seventeen years old. Since she has not reached adulthood, her mother, Yang Xia (age fifty), acted as her legal representative. She hired attorney Zhang Ding to file a lawsuit in the criminal division of the Second Special District Court, accusing Zhang Dayuan from Wuxi and his elder brother Zhang Zhirui, Zhang Boliang, and others of abandonment. The complaint reads: "Fraudulent marriage, disruption of family, request for arrest and prosecution, and request for incidental civil lawsuit to recover support and consolation money. The plaintiff, Xia, gave birth to a daughter, Xianfen. In the winter of last year, Zhang Dayuan, a wealthy merchant from Wuxi residing in Sichuan, proposed marriage through a matchmaker, intending to marry Xianfen as his wife. In March of this year, Xia personally went to Shanghai and met with Dayuan's elder brother Zhang Zhirui and Zhang Boliang. She inquired about Dayuan's character, family background, and financial situation. Zhirui and Boliang acknowledged that Dayuan was their younger brother and that he had shares in the father's Shenxin Textile Factory, as well as real estate and cash in Shanghai worth approximately 200,000 taels, which had not yet been divided. They assured her that after Dayuan married, he would be able to afford family expenses by drawing five to six hundred yuan per month from his share of the inheritance. Xia believed this to be true and returned to Sichuan. In June of the same year, Xianfen and Dayuan formally married in their hometown. Several months later, Dayuan returned to Shanghai first, promising to live with his elder brother in Shanghai for care. In September, the plaintiff, mother and daughter, along with two servants, brought their belongings to Shanghai and temporarily stayed at the Ping'an Hotel. They sought Zhang Dayuan without success. They contacted his elder brother Zhirui and Boliang, informing them of the reason for bringing the family to Shanghai. Zhirui rented a house for them at No. 8 Shengmuyuan Road and promised to inform Dayuan to come forward and arrange matters. If expenses were needed, they could be sent or drawn from Dayuan's inheritance. Unexpectedly, for two months, nothing was done, and Dayuan's whereabouts remained unknown, leaving the plaintiff stranded in Shanghai. Due to lack of funds, they could not move into the rented house. The defendant Dayuan should be held criminally liable for abandonment, which goes without saying. Tracing back to the origin, Xianfen and Dayuan's marriage was based on consultations with his brothers Zhirui and Boliang, who all claimed that Dayuan was their younger brother, how wealthy he was, and how he would have no worries about his livelihood before they agreed to the marriage. If the defendants had informed the plaintiffs of Dayuan's character earlier, they would not have wrongly married their young daughter to Dayuan. In their actions, the three brothers conspired to bring about the marriage through deception, which is clearly a violation of Article 310 of the Criminal Code. Therefore, the plaintiff requests the court to summon the defendants to court, pronounce them guilty, and punish them according to the law. Furthermore, Xianfen and Dayuan are legally married, making them members of the Zhang family. Therefore, they request an incidental civil lawsuit, and the defendants should be held liable for support obligations under Article 1114 of the Family Code, and order the defendants to pay a one-time support and consolation fee of 40,000 taels, to be received by the plaintiff Xianfen." The court, upon receiving the complaint, held a hearing on the previous day. First, the plaintiff's attorney presented the case, stating that Xianfen was three months pregnant. Zhang Dayuan testified that after the plaintiff and his mother came to Shanghai, a merchant rented a house for them and instructed the plaintiff to move in and live together, but the plaintiff and his mother ignored it and abandoned the opportunity themselves, and that it was not abandoned by the merchant. The merchant strongly objected to the plaintiff's request for consolation money. His lawyer argued on behalf of Zhang Zhirui that the merchant had been adopted out at a young age and had already severed his relationship with the Zhang family. Zhang Boliang stated that the merchant's family property had already been divided before his younger brother married the plaintiff and that there was evidence of this division. The merchant's marriage with the plaintiff had nothing to do with the merchant. After debate by the lawyers of both parties, Judge Luo Renji declared the end of the debate and sentenced the plaintiff's accusation of abandonment and incidental civil lawsuit to be dismissed together, and declared the defendants not guilty.

Zhuang Jihuai Favors Concubine, Suppresses Wife 142

▲ Accused of Neglecting Support

▲ Court Orders Mediation

Zhuang Jihuai of Ningbo married Zheng Liqing and lived in their hometown for eighteen years. Zhuang came to Shanghai to manage real estate and made considerable profits. However, feeling lonely as a sojourner, he took a young woman as a concubine, keeping her in a luxurious home and enjoying tender pleasures, neglecting his legal wife. Later, Mrs. Zheng learned of this in their hometown and came to Shanghai as well. At first, the legal wife and the concubine lived together, but as time went on, their disagreements deepened, and arguments arose frequently. Whenever the two women argued, Zhuang failed to mediate fairly, siding with the concubine and suppressing his wife. Increasingly angered, Mrs. Zheng rented a separate house. Unexpectedly, Zhuang soon cut off her living expenses, leaving her in dire straits. She was forced to file a petition with the First Special District Local Court, requesting that Zhuang Jihuai be summoned to court for mediation to continue providing monthly support to maintain her livelihood. However, despite repeated summons issued by the court, Zhuang persistently evaded them, making mediation impossible. Consequently, Mrs. Zheng formally filed a lawsuit against Zhuang for alimony and requested the pre-trial seizure of the defendant's assets, which was approved. Zhuang then urgently hired a lawyer to file a formal defense. Yesterday, Judge Yang presided over the court hearing. Both parties, accompanied by their lawyers, were present. Zhuang, with his eloquent tongue and skillful rhetoric, preempted the plaintiff's lawyer and the plaintiff herself, launching into a detailed account of his relationship with Zheng, from their marriage to the present situation, resembling a lecture. The judge, finding that much of his statement was irrelevant to the case, repeatedly stopped him, but he continued to speak volubly and somewhat plausibly. Judge Yang, noting that he had no intention of abandoning his wife, inquired whether he could provide the plaintiff with forty gold coins per month for living expenses. Although he did not deny it, he insisted on his poverty. However, according to the plaintiff's testimony, if the defendant were not wealthy, why would his concubine's residence be furnished entirely with rosewood furniture? Furthermore, the real estate company he managed was not closed down; it was only after the lawsuit was filed that he removed the signboard. She requested that the court not be misled by his false claims. Zhuang then continued, "I really have no funds to pay the plaintiff, but my elder brother can provide her with forty silver dollars per month." Zheng immediately countered, "Her brother is now in Ningbo; how can he give me the money?" Zhuang then retorted, "If the plaintiff does not want to go to Ningbo to receive the money, my younger brother can pay her." Hearing this, Zheng continued, "Although her younger brother used to run a silk shop in Shanghai, he is now unemployed and has no extra money to give me." The judge then ordered an adjournment, instructing both parties to discuss a settlement out of court and await further consideration.

Runaway Daughter-in-Law Unwilling to Return Home 143

▲ Sent to Court for Trial

Gong Xia, an old woman from Nanxiang, is fifty-one years old. She has one son and one daughter. Her son, A Da, is twenty-six years old and currently works as a senior steward for a foreigner. In the winter of the fifteenth year of the Republic, she arranged for her son to marry a village girl named Wu through a matchmaker. After their marriage, the couple's relationship was relatively harmonious. However, after only a year, Wu suddenly had a change of heart, falsely accusing her husband of neglecting her support. Subsequently, she packed up her clothes and disappeared without a trace. Although her mother-in-law and husband immediately launched a thorough search, her whereabouts remained unknown. Time flew by, and three years have now passed. Gong Xia, whose son now works in Shanghai, came to Shanghai in August this year and rented a room in a bungalow in Xiaoshadu, west of Shanghai, to search for her runaway daughter-in-law. It was not until the other day that she learned that Wu was hiding in No. 31, North Caojiazhai, Caojiadu, west of Shanghai. Ostensibly, she was working in a yarn factory to make a living, but in reality, she had become intimate with someone. Yesterday morning, Xia, accompanied by her younger daughter, went to the address and seized Wu, urging her to return home. Wu adamantly refused. They immediately called the police, who took her back to the Sixth District Police Station. According to Gong Xia's statement to the district chief, as mentioned above, Wu, who is twenty-five years old and from Nanxiang, stated that she was forced to flee to Shanghai to work and make a living because her husband neglected her support and subjected her to all kinds of abuse. It has been three years now. She heard that her husband has remarried. If she returns home, she will inevitably be abused even more. She really cannot bear the suffering and is therefore unwilling to return home with her mother-in-law. After hearing the statements, the district chief, considering the case of the runaway daughter-in-law unwilling to return, ordered that a written report be prepared and sent to the court for trial.

Reader's Correspondence

Opposing the Scattered Sale of Confiscated Japanese Goods and Questioning Mr. Xue Guangqian (High School Leisure) 159

In the 51st issue of Life Weekly, Volume 6, Mr. Xue Guangqian had an article expressing his views on the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association Design Committee's draft on how to dispose of confiscated Japanese goods. The draft has never been made public. Outsiders only heard that its content was roughly the same as that proposed by the business community's Economic Severance Association. Seeing Mr. Xue's letter now, it can further confirm that the Anti-Japanese Association Design Committee's draft is indeed a scattered sale plan, not a centralized public sale. "Unconditional scattered sale is certainly a malicious accusation," but scattered sale is still scattered sale, only a conditional one. I believe that the current point of contention is the two paths of scattered sale and centralized public sale. The right and wrong are clear, and there is no need to hesitate or waver. There is absolutely no room for compromise.

What kind of conditions are involved in the so-called conditional scattered sale? When implementing scattered sales, how will you prevent the many unregistered Japanese goods and future smuggled goods from taking the opportunity to be sold? The Anti-Japanese Association Design Committee has proposed no more than three preventive measures: (1) issuing sales licenses, (2) stamping each item, and (3) establishing separate account books when selling. Mr. Xue said, "Its preventive and sales methods are extremely cautious." In my opinion, these methods can be said to be a kind of deception that can only fool children. Suppose you have a bolt of confiscated Japanese cloth. As long as you register with the Anti-Japanese Association and get a sales license, you can openly sell it. Who has the time to ask you if you have a sales license and to distinguish whether your sales license is genuine? Moreover, the sales license and the goods being sold are not inseparable. One sales license can be used repeatedly many times. With a bolt of registered Japanese cloth, you can sell dozens or hundreds of bolts of Japanese cloth. Hidden smuggled goods can certainly be gradually sold off. On the one hand, you can still import goods from the Japanese. The so-called "inventory" will come from a source and will never be sold out. "Stamping each item" is even more ridiculous. May I ask how you stamp Japanese sugar, Japanese coal, and Japanese seafood? How do you stamp it on the outside of the package? What happens after the package is removed? How do you use one package dozens of times? The value of the Japanese goods confiscated in Shanghai is as high as tens of millions, and the number of items is over one hundred million. Suppose the Anti-Japanese Association sends dozens of trustworthy staff to stamp each piece of cloth, each fish, and each piece of coal (not to mention each grain of sugar), and gives it a stamp. Even if dozens of people work at the same time, it will probably take more than half a year. Anyone can forge these dozens of wooden stamps. Within a few days, they can be transformed into thousands. The general public, seeing a few blurred words, will think it is an Anti-Japanese Association stamp. As for whether the stamp is genuine or fake, we are not seal experts. How can we distinguish it? The method of establishing separate account books is even more inexplicable. If a merchant prepares an account book but does not use it, what can you do? You can't possibly send someone to supervise him in every store. What cunning merchant who sells smuggled goods would honestly record it in the account book and wait for you to report him? There is absolutely no such fool in the world.

Scattered sales have not yet been implemented, and it is already impossible to prevent the leakage of Japanese goods. Everyone, try to imagine what the anti-Japanese movement will look like if scattered sales are actually implemented. The so-called sales license and stamping of each item will become a kind of talisman for unscrupulous merchants. Before, it was done stealthily. Now, they can sell openly and brazenly. Registered goods and unregistered goods, old stock and newly imported goods, will inevitably become indistinguishable. The work of inspection will also be impossible. Once this dam is broken, Japanese goods will definitely flood in like a tide, inundating all of China. Months of effort and sacrifice will only create an opportunity for unscrupulous merchants to make a fortune. If you must put the confiscated Japanese goods up for sale, there is no second way to go besides centralized public sale. Merchants who want to recover their costs can find ways within the scope of centralized public sale. Why do some people insist on adopting that scattered sale system that is impossible to prevent? People who do not want to steal will never object to others closing the door and locking the box. Boycotting Japanese goods is our nation's only remaining weapon. We cannot listen to a small number of people and easily lose it. Before the Anti-Japanese Association's final plan is decided (the draft mentioned above has been temporarily put aside), we should all stand up and closely supervise them. All groups should have a serious expression.

▲ Postscript: Everyone knows the evils of the scattered sale system. Those who cannot profit will not advocate scattered sales. Even with centralized public sale, there must be a proper method. You must not sell all the inventory as much as possible. I advocate a phased sale solution. Now, I will excerpt a section from the letter I wrote to the Anti-Japanese Association below.

"... The reason why previous boycotts of Japanese goods failed was due to the unrestricted sale of Japanese goods that had already entered the country. During the boycott period, it was carried out with great fanfare. The source of Japanese goods was temporarily cut off, but there were still many inventories on the market that could meet the temporary needs (before each boycott, merchants would rush to import large quantities of Japanese goods, and there would be no worry about not having goods to sell for several months). When the inventory was about to be cleared, the boycott was canceled invisibly, and large quantities of Japanese goods could be imported again to make up for the shortage of Japanese goods on the market. This is why Japanese goods imports must increase greatly before the boycott, and Japanese goods imports must increase greatly after the boycott. In the long run, Japanese goods imports have not decreased compared to normal times... If the goods confiscated this time can be preserved until the boycott is over, and then put up for sale again, then there will be a sudden increase in Japanese goods on the market at that time, and there will be no need to import large quantities from Japan. During the boycott period, Japanese goods will disappear from the market, and their sales will be taken away by Western goods or domestic goods. The Japanese will have no way to compensate for this kind of loss. If you boycott for one year, there will be the effect of one year. If you boycott for two years, there will be the effect of two years. It will not be like the complete failure of the past. Even for the sake of the merchants' costs, the goods imported before the boycott cannot be sealed forever. As a last resort, there is also a compromise solution. How can you rashly unload the confiscated goods on the market and ruin the future of the boycott movement? I have proposed two strategies for the disposal of confiscated goods: (1) after six months, conduct a centralized public sale and allow merchants to use this inventory as collateral; (2) conduct a limited sale, for example, goods that can be sold in one month during normal times should be sold in four months, selling one-quarter each month. In this way, three-quarters of the Japanese goods market will be taken away by goods from other countries. The second method seems easier to implement..."

Letters Received 162

To the Editor, Regarding the Shanghai Municipal Business Transportation Committee's merchants association representative meeting reported in your newspaper's local news on the 20th of this month, there was mention of the iron industry and the third temporary motion included the proposal from the iron industry and other industries. Our industry was unaware of the Business Transportation Committee meeting and did not send a representative to attend. However, we heard that Mr. Lu Peizhi went to the meeting upon receiving a letter, but left shortly after sitting down. He did not propose any matters, and it was Mr. Lu's individual action, not representing our entire industry. We fear that the rumors are inaccurate and request a correction to ensure accuracy. Sincerely, Shanghai Iron Industry Association, December 20, 1931. To the Editor, Today I saw an article in your newspaper (Business Transportation Committee news) with the phrase "Qiu Liangyu of the Second District City Federation and others attended." I went yesterday as an individual to listen in. I had just signed in and was about to enter when a friend came out and said that the meeting was about to end, so there was no need to go in. Therefore, I left with him and did not attend, nor did I represent the Second District City Federation. Please investigate and correct this matter. Sincerely, Qiu Liangyu, December 20.

To the Editor, Upon reviewing your newspaper's local news section on the 20th of this month, there was a report on the meeting of the First District Electrical Workers' Union, which stated that the Municipal Ink Industry Union participated. Our union did not send any representatives to participate, which is inconsistent with the facts. We hereby issue a statement and request a prompt correction. Sincerely, Shanghai Municipal Ink Industry Workers' Union. To the Editor, Yesterday I read in your newspaper's local news section about the declaration of various labor unions supporting the Party Affairs Improvement Association. The Sixth District Qin Industry Union was listed, which caused great consternation. There is only one legitimate organization of Qin industry workers in this city, and there are no other organizations. Our association was not consulted about supporting the Party Affairs Improvement Association beforehand, and it is obvious that someone is impersonating us in an attempt to confuse the public. We hereby request that your newspaper grant a correction. Sincerely, Shanghai Qin Industry Labor Union.

Since the market weakened at the beginning of the week, the minimum price for January was 639.5 taels. As for overseas silver markets, the trends diverged, with British silver slightly declining and American silver rising. Chinese merchants engaged in both hedging and arbitrage, gradually narrowing the spread from over fifty taels to around thirty taels.
