Securities Market: Bond Market Meanders Last Week 166

During the past week (from December 14th to 19th), the bond market conditions of the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange in this city were quite active in the spot market, with lively trading. Except for the 96 Public Bonds, all bond types were opened. The total turnover for the week was 204,100 yuan, including 46,900 yuan for the 1919 Customs Bonds, 43,000 yuan for Consolidated Tax Bonds, 37,000 yuan for Salt Tax Bonds, 29,500 yuan for the 1920 Customs Bonds, 19,000 yuan for the 1919 Charity Bonds, and 4,000 to 5,000 yuan for each of the others. Additionally, bonds that had not been traded for a long time, such as Post-War Military Relief and Disaster Relief Bonds, each opened at 1,000 yuan at the end of the week. Futures were generally quiet, and the market was very idle, but the January futures for each bond type had all been opened, and turnover increased slightly. The average daily turnover for the past week was over 6 million yuan, except for Tuesday, which was only over 1.6 million yuan, and Monday, which was only over 3.4 million yuan. Thursday reached over 8.6 million yuan. The total turnover for the week was 32.11 million yuan, an increase of approximately 11 million yuan compared to the previous week, including 2.735 million yuan for the December Consolidated Tax Bonds, 2.5 million yuan for the January Consolidated Tax Bonds, 3.1 million yuan for the December Salt Tax Bonds, 2.005 million yuan for the January Salt Tax Bonds, 3.01 million yuan for the December 1920 Customs Bonds, 2.055 million yuan for the January 1920 Customs Bonds, 2.055 million yuan for the December 1920 Restructured Bonds, 1.15 million yuan for the January 1920 Restructured Bonds, 2.065 million yuan for the December 1919 Charity Bonds, 1.095 million yuan for the January 1919 Charity Bonds, 2.055 million yuan for the December 1919 Customs Bonds, 950,000 yuan for the January 1919 Customs Bonds, 2.47 million yuan for the December Disbandment Bonds, 60,000 yuan for the January Disbandment Bonds, 1.67 million yuan for the December Reorganization Bonds, 850,000 yuan for the January Reorganization Bonds, 460,000 yuan for the December 6% Bonds, 15,000 yuan for the January 6% Bonds, 575,000 yuan for the December Customs Duty Bonds, 65,000 yuan for the January Customs Duty Bonds, 675,000 yuan for the December 1996 Public Bonds, and 95,000 yuan for the January 1996 Public Bonds. In terms of trends, the restriction of price limits prevented free development, and market conditions were also affected. Market sentiment was chaotic regarding the bond market, and most people were observing. There were no large-scale inflows or outflows, and the supply and demand were balanced. The market prices of each bond type did not change significantly. Looking at the changes over the week, due to the hasty conclusion of the League of Nations on Monday without any significant achievements, and the continued implementation of aggressive policies by the Japanese without any remorse, the market was pessimistic about the future. Although there were no large-scale outflows, the buying interest was depressed, and demand was low. The prices trended downward from the previous weekend, and except for the 6% Bonds, Customs Duty Bonds, 1996 Public Bonds, and Disbandment Bonds, all other bond types fell to the predetermined minimum price limit. On Tuesday, all prices reached the price limit, and trading could not continue, so there were few inflows or outflows and minor fluctuations. However, on Wednesday and Thursday, there were political changes in the country. Ning and Yue cooperated, and Chiang and Zhang resigned successively. The Japanese cabinet was also reorganized, and the situation was refreshed for a while. Market sentiment was excited and optimistic about the future. Investment and buying were active, and demand increased. The market prices of each bond type rebounded sharply, with increases of approximately two yuan. The market situation suddenly became lively. However, on Friday and Saturday, the market slumped again. Various parties, in view of the domestic situation, noted that many things were not yet in place. Although the Japanese cabinet had been reorganized, the intention to invade remained unchanged. The increase in troops and aggression showed us that it was even worse. Therefore, people were uneasy, and prices trended downward again, gradually falling. By the weekend, each bond type had fallen close to the price limit again. As a result, there were only fluctuations of two or three yuan for the whole week, and compared to the previous week, the overall decline continued, but the amount was still small. It was noted that various parties found the price limit inconvenient, and had discussed with the Ministry of Finance to cancel it. However, if the market situation is not remedied and buying interest is encouraged, it is feared that there will be no turnaround for the time being. Free Talk

Memories of the East Haired 171

— Yanzi

When Yu Dongfa was young, he was weak and sickly. He followed Mr. Li to Shanghai and sought out famous doctors, both Chinese and foreign, to diagnose and treat his madness. At that time, his cousin, Huang Mengwan, recommended him to a Japanese female doctor named Maruhashi for examination. Maruhashi was a middle-aged woman with a repulsive face, wearing wide sleeves and wooden clogs, a laughable sight. She held a stethoscope and examined his entire body, sometimes in deep thought, sometimes lost in contemplation, muttering to herself, not knowing what she was saying. She gave him a small bottle of medicinal water to apply to the affected area, which showed some effectiveness. It was probably a kind of insecticidal medicinal water. The following year, relations between China and Japan deteriorated, and Yu's madness recurred. He returned to Maruhashi for treatment, and the consultation fee suddenly doubled (2 yuan for a consultation, 4 yuan for a house call). Her attitude also changed drastically, becoming arrogant and unbearable, a stark contrast to her servile demeanor during his first visit. Although Yu was young, he tasted her contempt and was filled with anger. He stormed out and vowed never to see the ugly face of a Japanese woman again, preferring to be afflicted with madness. Later, he was cured by a Mr. Ding from Zhenjiang (a specialist in madness). His uncle once stroked Yu's back and smiled, saying, "This child is stubborn."

Do Not Remove Garden Grass: Zhaifu's Chat

Zhaifu Union 172

"In the latest issue of "Love," a special column of Zhaifu's chat, "Green Window Full of Herbs," was written last month. Is the title "Is it True or False?" written by you?"

"No."

"The name "Green Window Full of Herbs" certainly comes from the line of poetry "Green window full of herbs, do not remove." Aren't "Green Window Full of Zhaifu" and "Do Not Remove Garden Grass Zhaifu" the same person?"

"Not the same person. I don't have his good fortune."

"What good fortune does he have?"

"His eyes are fortunate, he can watch movies."

"Then who is Green Window Full of Zhaifu? What is his surname?"

"I don't know who he is, but I know his color."

"What color is he? White? Red? Yellow? Black?"

"He's green; we can call him Green Zhaifu. If my surname is "Do Not," then perhaps his surname is "Green.""

"Now that you have this Green Zhaifu, you won't be lonely anymore."

"Right! There is also a Do Not Remove Garden Grass Zhaifu in the Republic of China Daily. We already have three comrades."

"I think since you already have three comrades, you can organize a Zhaifu Union. You can mutually elect the following officers:

Executive Minister: Do Not Remove Garden Grass Zhaifu

Organization Minister: Green Window Full of Zhaifu

Propaganda Minister: Do Not Remove Garden Grass Zhaifu"

"Good, let's organize, and do a big cleanup, removing all the filth, garbage, dust, and microorganisms, to clean up a clean and bright house."

Anecdotes of Liu Yongfu 173

— Qing Qu

Around the seventh or eighth year of the Guangxu reign (1881-1882), the French wanted to implement trade on the Red River. At that time, there was a leader of the Black Flag Party, Liu Yongfu, in name. In fact, he was a valiant general of the Taiping Army, originally from Qinzhou, Guangdong. In his youth, he wandered abroad, living near the border of Yunnan and Vietnam. As he grew older, he became a merchant in Vietnam, frequently traveling between Xuan Quang and An Binh. He generously distributed wealth and gathered a group of loyal and dedicated followers, numbering several hundred. When bandits rose up and invaded Bao Thang in Xinghua, the authorities of Xinghua, admiring Liu Yongfu as a hero, invited him to pacify the area. He then stationed troops in Bao Thang. Later, the Vietnamese King heard of Liu Yongfu’s accumulated merits and appointed him as the Deputy Commissioner of the Three Provinces (Xuan Quang, Xinghua, and Shanxi), entrusting him with the responsibility of defending the territory. When General Feng Zicai arrived in Vietnam, he found that Liu Yongfu was his fellow townsman and that Liu Yongfu possessed a heroic and outstanding spirit, he intended to bring him back to China. It was rumored that Feng had granted him the rank of a fifth-grade official. However, since Liu Yongfu had already been appointed to an official position and was heavily relied upon, this never came to pass.

As Commissioner, Liu Yongfu was allowed to collect taxes to support his troops. The French used this as an excuse, claiming it hindered trade, and successively captured Hanoi and other places. The troops stationed in Shanxi under Liu Yongfu were extremely fierce. Furthermore, the Governor of Yunnan, Cen Yuying, provided him with military supplies. Therefore, in his battles against the French, he repeatedly reported great victories to the court. The French feared him and instead sent troops to invade China. Vietnam also requested assistance. Consequently, Li Shaoquan was ordered to lead troops to assist. However, he first arrived in Tianjin and had already made an agreement with the French envoy, Binhai. At that time, Peng Yulin was in charge of coastal defense in Guangdong, while Tang Jiong, the Governor of Yunnan, was stationed in Shanxi, and Xu Tingxu, the Governor of Guangxi, was stationed in Beining. All were dismissed from their positions and arrested for questioning. Liu Yongfu's troops were also defeated. The French naval commander, Fulu Nuo, intended to drive out the Black Flag Army, but Shaoquan suppressed this and did not report it to the Emperor. Later, Liu Yongfu accepted the Qing court’s offer of amnesty and was also given the rank of Commissioner with the notation. He then recaptured the Three Provinces. Commentators at the time said, "The affair of the Southern Barbarians cannot be accomplished. If he loses, he will be annihilated by the French. If he wins, he will be resented by the Chinese generals. Retreating and advancing, he is in a difficult situation." There were those who privately felt concerned for Liu Yongfu. This was not without insight.

Alas, Liu Yongfu, with a solitary and isolated army, uniquely raised the banner of righteousness.

What I Saw and Heard 174

— Da Wei

Recently, I went to the countryside. A group of people surrounded me and asked about current affairs. I said, "The country is about to be destroyed." They said, "The flood has receded. This year's rice harvest is still good. How can the country be destroyed?"

××××

Students in big cities are rioting with strikes. Stores in small cities are rioting with market strikes. The former wants to force the authorities to save the country. The latter forces the authorities not to save the country.

××××

"If you boycott Japanese goods, Japan will naturally send troops to fight. It's like scratching an itch on a tiger's head, bringing trouble upon yourself." An old man was smugly lecturing. I suddenly understood the root cause of the country's destruction.

Resisting the French army with a mere few thousand newly gathered troops, repeatedly thwarting a powerful enemy, beheading generals and capturing flags, pursuing the defeated, causing anyone with any patriotism to rise up at the sound of his name, was unprecedented since the border affairs. Yet, the Qing court disparaged him, suspecting him of seeking undeserved credit or embellishing his reports as untrue and exaggerated, akin to causing panic. Therefore, during the Sino-French War, Liu Yongfu could only win and could not afford to lose. He could only advance and could not retreat. This was no different from abandoning a man of great talent and strategy to the jaws of a tiger, watching him perish without being able to help him. At the time, concerned individuals said, "This is enough to make all talented people in the world weep." This was truly not a false statement. In my youth, hearing Liu Yongfu's name, my ears would tremble. His reputation was no less than that of General Ma today. In Shanghai, photography was not yet prevalent, so among the Western-made portraits that were hung in homes, besides Zeng, Zuo, and Li, there was only Liu Yongfu. Observing his appearance, he was not yet fifty years old, his mustache had not yet fully grown, he looked like a handsome young man. He appeared physically weak, but his eyebrows and eyes revealed an extraordinary spirit. Initially, I thought he would be a towering and extraordinary figure, unlike ordinary people, but I did not expect that a naturally endowed hero could not be measured by appearances. Even so, the more I consider Liu Yongfu's time and circumstances, and the difficulty and hardship of his position, the more I cannot help but worry for General Ma today. Alas.

Gao Junshan's Talk on National Crisis After Returning from Europe and America (4) 176

— Ji Ping

4. In terms of the United Nations' personnel and administration, there is absolutely no equality. The League of Nations has three major organs: (1) the Secretariat, (2) the International Court of Justice, and (3) the International Labor Office. It is said that there are over a thousand employees in these three major organs. British and French nationals are the most numerous. There are only four Chinese in the Secretariat, and their positions are not important. There is not a single Chinese in the Labor Office. There is only Wang Chonghui in the International Court of Justice, which is relatively more important. There are also many Japanese, and they hold key positions such as various ministerial posts. The most regrettable thing is that sometimes the League of Nations consults Japan whenever it needs to inquire about Chinese affairs. The Japanese take this opportunity to use their glib tongues to conduct all sorts of counter-propaganda. It is truly absurd.

China's obligations to the League of Nations are in the same proportion as other countries, but the rights it enjoys are uniquely few. The government should protest against this unequal phenomenon.

We should have known long ago that the League of Nations is unreliable. We should not only know it now. Moreover, we should not still be timid and indecisive under such severe military pressure from Japan, relying on the League of Nations as our great support. That is why our diplomacy has suffered a complete defeat. There are many people who advocate withdrawing from the League of Nations now. In fact, considering the current situation, there are reasons why we cannot withdraw immediately.

(A) According to the Covenant of the League of Nations, any member state wishing to withdraw must give two years' advance notice. It cannot be decided on a whim.

(B) Before withdrawing, it must fulfill its obligations to the League of Nations. For example, our country still owes a lot in membership fees. We cannot withdraw until our obligations are fulfilled.

According to this situation, we really cannot withdraw. Even if we could withdraw, I don't think we should withdraw. Our country would be even more isolated internationally, and Japan would be able to act even more arbitrarily and unscrupulously. Like in recent conferences, Japanese representatives often found themselves at a loss for words and reason in front of a large audience, embarrassing the United States and all nations. Although it did not actually cause any damage, it was still embarrassing. Moreover, our country has always lacked the tools for international propaganda. The current Eastern Provinces Incident is largely due to the existence of the League of Nations, which focused the attention of countries around the world, and the truth has been revealed to the world. Therefore, joining the League of Nations is certainly not beneficial to us, but withdrawing from the League of Nations is even more beneficial to Japan. This is my humble opinion on why we should not withdraw from the League of Nations. However, after this major setback, our views on the League of Nations should undergo a major change, and from now on, we must know how to fully utilize the League of Nations so that we do not waste such a huge amount of annual membership fees.

Madame Mallory's success is of course half due to her talent. Her beauty, her courage, her intelligence. Going on an Expedition 177

— A Member of the Youth Support Ma Group, First Platoon

(4) Leaving Nanxiang

Very early today (the 11th), we faintly heard the emergency assembly call. The comrades all woke up nimbly, competing to go to the meeting place to receive the commander's mobilization order. Before long, we were all prepared and set off towards Kunshan. At this time, the sun had not yet shone on the earth. The withered yellow roadside grass was ravaged by the night's cold dew, as if unable to bear its weariness. However, looking back at the state of the country, it was even worse than the roadside grass. My heart was filled with indescribable sadness.

At noon, we arrived at Anting. We were received by the Sanxian Rural Normal School, and the commander gave thanks to all sectors of society at the welcoming ceremony, and explained the purpose of this trip. After lunch, we set off to the west.

When we arrived in Kunshan, the county party headquarters and all sectors of society sent representatives to greet us at the station. Huge white cloth banners were hung on the station and along the road, all written with slogans welcoming or praising us. We stayed overnight at the County Middle School in the evening.

The scenery here is very good, and the road administration is also good. The customs are especially simple and honest. When the locals saw the coffin of the regimental spirit of our team, they were all surprised and whispered to each other. Some old and young men and women who understood our determination to eliminate the Japanese felt all the more unbearable when they saw this frightening thing, and frequently wiped their tears with handkerchiefs.

Military life is very unique. We do not feel its bitterness at all, but instead, our appetites have greatly increased, and we eat several more bowls of coarse rice.

Sharing the Same Hatred with You (18) 178

— Gu Mingdao

Chapter 4: Righteousness Above Family

"Ten thousand li to the battlefield, crossing mountains as if flying. The northern air transmits the sound of metal clappers, the cold light shines on iron armor." Zhongshu had already felt this scene and this emotion. Unexpectedly, Peng Meiguo's army arrived on the banks of the L River, and the H Province defense army on the opposite side had already destroyed the river bridge. The surging water was very vast, and it was impossible to fly across it for a while. They could only temporarily set up camp and wait. Peng Meiguo's headquarters was located in a Tiandao village more than ten li away from the river bridge. Peng Meiguo talked with his chief of staff and the Japanese officers for a long time in the evening. Feeling somewhat tired, he was about to go to sleep when he saw his daughter Zhongshu burst in from outside. Meiguo asked, "The weather is very cold, and the north wind is strong. Why haven't you gone to sleep yet?" Zhongshu said, "Hua Naiqiang has a secret matter to report to Father." Meiguo smiled slightly, "What secret does he have?" Just as he said the word "secret," the word "matter" had not yet been uttered, Hua Naiqiang had already jumped in from outside, holding a pistol high in his hand, aimed at Peng Meiguo and shouted, "Traitor, don't move!" Where did Peng Meiguo expect such a move? He was already frightened stiff. At this time, Hua Naiqiang was awe-inspiring, and said again, "Traitor, you are so muddled-headed, how can you be worthy of the country, worthy of your compatriots? You are leading this nameless army to serve as a tool for the tiger. You have lost all conscience. I have come for the sake of the country to carry out your death sentence. Today is your last day!" Peng Meiguo was greatly shocked. Just as he was about to shout loudly, he heard the sound of a gunshot, and Peng Meiguo had already fallen into a pool of blood. The two guards outside heard the sound and entered, but Hua Naiqiang shot them down one by one, finishing them off. Looking back at Zhongshu, he saw that she had already fallen on that old thief's body, sobbing. Naiqiang could not help but kneel down to her and said, "Madam, please forgive me. I had no choice but to do this. Now please stop your weeping. We need to discuss the aftermath." Zhongshu wiped away her tears and stood up, saying, "I have already agreed. This matter is for the sake of the country and the people. What is your fault? I only regret that my father was muddled-headed and senile, and was taken advantage of. That is why there is today's result. As his daughter, I could not persuade him to change his mind or stop his act of treason, which makes me deeply sad. Alas, since I cannot be Shen Yunying, nor can I be Gou Guan Niang, what else is there to say? Now, all matters should be carried out according to the plan that Brother Naiqiang agreed on before." Hua Naiqiang could not help but sigh to the sky. At this time, the horses of the Hu were neighing in the wind, and the sound of swords and fighting was silent. The scene before them was only solemn, and the lamplight was also dim. The two of them stood there, both feeling a special sensation.

Scattered Notes on a Concert 179

— Ms. Zhiyin

I saw advertisements twice, saying that a world-renowned Spanish violin master was performing in Shanghai. I didn't go the first time, but I did the second time, but it was already full. The third time, I rushed there alone at 8:30, but I still came in vain because I hadn't reserved a seat and there were no tickets left. But I decided to wait a while and see what happened. Sure enough, there were many foreigners waiting for tickets just like me who hadn't reserved a seat. So a Chinese ticket seller walked into the ticket window and started selling standing tickets, signing "Stand" on each ticket stub. I bought a standing ticket like that too.

The ushers were foreign girls, probably eighteen or nineteen years old, who seemed to be Russian. They were wearing plain khaki tops and tight, dark blue skirts.

I was standing by the railing behind the last seat. I treated the railing as a chair. Many foreigners and Chinese who had later standing tickets wanted to grab my spot but couldn't. I didn't leave from the moment I went in until the end. The girls came and went, ushering people in. Sometimes they bumped into my body, and I could hear a small, high-pitched "Sorry", and at the same time I could see a momentary cordial smile.

There were also plump and fat old women, as well as pot-bellied rich men, with the glitter of gold rings on their fingers and gold watch chains hanging on their bellies. Most of the young women had snow-white and tall fur collars and shiny black coats, with the long corners of their evening dresses trailing on the floor. Westerners respect all kinds of art very much. Look, they are going to a concert, and they are all wearing stiff evening dresses. There were also young men with long hair covering their heads, with eyes that seemed to have infinite thoughts, as if trying to explore something, but most of these were Chinese.

Several plump foreign ladies walked in, and a young man stood up from his seat to greet them. The foreign ladies stretched out their wrinkled hands, and the young man kissed each hand.

My watch pointed to 9:20. All the lights in the hall went out, and the electric lights in front of the stage were particularly bright. Then there was no sound at all. The air was completely quiet, so quiet that even breathing felt uneasy. I was so breathless by this silence that I didn't dare to breathe.

Heifetz, with his left hand holding a violin and his right hand holding a bow, walked out from the left of the stage. Two other people walked out at the same time behind him. The whole audience clapped and applauded. All three were wearing swallowtail evening dresses and bowed deeply to the audience at a ninety-degree angle.

The stage was very high. Behind it was a large gray curtain. A piano and a chair were quietly placed there long ago. The electric light shone on the piano surface, and then from the piano surface to people's eyelids. This was simply a picture, a clear and beautiful design picture.

Heifetz was a short, middle-aged man with very little hair. I was too far away to see clearly. His deep eyes were gentle and peaceful, and his manners were completely regular ninety-degree right angles, with an ironed evening dress.

The pianist was already half a hundred years old, with hair that seemed to be gray. He was hunched over, with his right foot stepping on the pedal and his left foot resting behind him in a human-like shape. His eyes were focused on the score, waiting for Heifetz's performance order. And in his consciousness, he didn't seem to know what was happening.

The other person was turning the pages of the music for the pianist.

There was no automation at all.

The piano was the first to sound, followed by the thin sounds of the violin.

The whole hall was completely quiet, except for the music, no one dared to make any noise.

The first piece was Beethoven's Ninth Symphony. The piano accompanied the violin, mixing and playing together, from slow and quiet to fast and urgent, from light and thin to agile and quick... Then, in the wave-like vibrations of the whole room, all emotions were attracted, instantly making you forget yourself, lose consciousness, your heart beating for it, your face burning for it. Sometimes it was so sharp that you couldn't hear the sound, and you were so breathless that you couldn't breathe, your emotions were being driven to the highest point.

The piece was divided into three short sections, each section lasting a few minutes. After the sections, there was a rest, and many more latecomers were standing outside the door. Some people walked out one after another, probably because they were too suffocated and went out to get some air. The sound was still very quiet, with none of the noise of a theater. The people who came in later made no sound at all. The women walked on tiptoe, and the men, when they walked, didn't hear any sound at all. Then I noticed if they were wearing rubber-heeled shoes.

During the rest, several plump foreign ladies walked in, and a young man stood up from his seat to greet them. The foreign ladies stretched out their wrinkled hands, and the young man kissed each hand.

The rests were a total of two times. When the third music began, it was a quiet tune, but perhaps because of the hazy effect of a preconceived psychology, I felt that the feeling of the first session of the three concerts was the best and the impression was the deepest.

Every time a piece was finished, there was a burst of applause, and the applause was continuous. Then Heifetz and the pianist came out together and bowed several times to the audience. Sometimes Heifetz came out for a long time, and sometimes the bow was in the shape of a snake, quickly pointing its head downwards and then gradually raising it upwards, while the body also bent like this. Sometimes Heifetz had to come out and bow twice before the applause could stop.

After the last piece was finished, Heifetz and the pianist went back in. I didn't know if it was the end. Looking at the program, it was already over, but no one moved, and the applause was still noisy. Then Heifetz and the pianist went on stage again. This may have been a common custom in the West, that you can ask to hear an extra piece after the end of the piece.

The light and crisp tune of the violin played another piece. I immediately put on my coat, but people still hadn't moved, and the applause was still continuing. The applause of a young foreign man in the front row on the right was so loud that my ears were almost deaf. Several Chinese women had already stood up. I was a few foreigners who had walked to the door, and some people had already walked out.

Heifetz came out again and bowed, a ninety-degree bow, a snake-shaped bow, and then started the violin again, adding the slender bow to the strings. This may have been a small piece, a completely light, floating scale.

There was another burst of applause, mixed with a kind of floating shout, shouted in English, meaning to come again. Several Chinese people were also shouting, shouting the same as the foreigners.

The people in the front row had already stood up, followed by the people in the middle row. I immediately stood up too.

I passed through the crisscrossing cars, and it was already twelve o'clock at night.

The Waiter 180

— Cheng

It was almost four o'clock. I, Bin, and Xin happened to walk past the City God Temple, and Xin suggested, "We haven't had vegetarian fried noodles for a long time. How about going for a meal? Anyway, it's snack time now."

"Okay, okay," Bin and I both agreed, feeling that it was true, we hadn't tasted vegetarian fried noodles that were as delicious as meat fried noodles for a long time. At the same time, our stomachs were rumbling a bit. The three of us walked towards ××× in unison.

The dishes at ××× are said to be lighter and fresher than other places,

and the portions are not small, so when we are in the City God Temple and want to eat vegetarian dishes and noodles, we must go to ×××. Although there are many vegetarian restaurants in the City God Temple.

We slowly walked up the stairs of the ××× restaurant and saw that there were not many people eating, so we casually sat down at a table by the window.

A very fat waiter, seeing us sitting down, rushed over, dusted the table with a white cloth on his shoulder a few times, and then took out chopsticks while saying very politely, "Miss, what dishes do you want?"

"A stir-fry..." I was slowly saying, when Xin stopped me, "We only need two bowls of Three Delicacies Fried Noodles."

The fat waiter, hearing "two bowls of fried noodles," turned around and walked to the stairs, shouting what we wanted loudly.

After he shouted, he poured three cups of tea. At this time, he was not as happy as before, he was almost wearing a straight face, putting the three cups of tea on the table and walking away.

Bin took a cup, raised it and said, "Look, there are a lot of dirty dregs in this tea. I'm going to exchange it for a cup of plain water. Do you want it too?"

Xin and I shook our heads and said, "We don't want tea or plain water."

Bin then raised his hand and said to the fat waiter standing on the side, "Come, change a cup of tea."

"What?" he stood in front of him very unhappily.

"This tea is very dirty, go and exchange it for a cup of plain water."

"Plain water is the same as this cup of tea, because this tea is also made with plain water." He made an indifferent expression, with his hands hanging at his sides, not showing any intention to exchange it, his attitude was very cold, motionless staring at Bin.

"Then don't worry about whether it's the same or not, just go and exchange it for a cup of plain water." I said slightly angrily, he glanced at me askance, also slightly angrily, poured the cup of tea into the spittoon beside our table, and then quickly walked away.

"This kind of waiter is really snobbish, he initially thought we were big spenders, so he treated us very politely, but when he found out that we were only eating one or two bowls of fried noodles, he was greatly disappointed and made this contemptuous attitude," Bin said.

"Although we are not afraid of his scorn, I think we should also stir-fry a few dishes to eat, what do you think?" I said, when I thought that it was rare for us to walk past the City God Temple.

"Okay, then what dishes do you like to eat?... Do you like stir-fried yam?" Xin looked at us.

We ordered a few dishes, then Xin waved and shouted, "Come!" This time, the waiter probably already knew that we were going to order a few dishes, he seemed to be less contemptuous of us than before.

"Stir-fry a few more dishes, a stir-fried yam, a stir-fried vegetable heart, a stir-fried assorted vegetables, half-sold is fine." The waiter showed a slight smile, nodding repeatedly and saying, "Understood, understood." This time, he seemed to be very respectful to us.

The dishes were brought one by one, and we ate them one by one. Bin had the smallest appetite, he was the first to stop eating, sitting next to us and waiting. At that time, the fat waiter came again, swaying, he first handed Bin a hot steaming towel and then said, "Do you still want plain water?" His peaceful attitude and words seemed to be asking for forgiveness for his rudeness just now.

After we had finished eating, we called him to calculate the money, "Thirty-one, forty-eight, fifty-three... including small accounts, a total of two yuan, thirty-five cents." He calculated very quickly.

We paid him two yuan and forty cents, and told him not to give us the change, he said humbly, "Miss, thank you." As we straightened our clothes and started to walk down the stairs,

"There are many of these lowly people. Getting a few more coins is like a greedy dog getting a piece of beef from a stranger's hand, it will wag its tail and show its diligence," Xin sighed, after walking out of ×××.

"Ah, why should people be slaves to money? Having money will definitely also get troubles. The waiter just now thanked us, but we coldly didn't even turn our heads back, as if we hadn't heard it. Just think, isn't this also embarrassing him?"

"But you don't know if he would rather be embarrassed than not get money," I said, while also sympathizing with the waiter, because he was originally this kind of person. Only getting money, he is willing to endure anything. What person is struggling without money?"

Movie Sketches by Lu Mengshu 183

Spring Love Holiday

If society is corrupt, it should be criticized. If youth is decadent, it should also be criticized. Because this is like the "one word of condemnation" in the Spring and Autumn Annals, making ugliness nowhere to hide, nowhere to be concealed, and nakedly presented before people, giving them such an ugly object to fiercely impose the most severe surveillance, and can also give both sides a new opportunity for improvement, making the corrupt aware of innovation and eliminating the influence on urban civilization, making the decadent stand firm and refuse to abandon themselves from humanity. So-called urban civilization is built on people's reason, emotion, passion, and material things, and absolutely does not allow social corruption or youthful decadence to shake its foundation. If it unfortunately reaches this point, artists must quickly rise up to realize the mission of art to seek all improvements. "Spring Love" (Holiday), a film recognized as very successful in the American film industry, its theme is built on such a concept.

America, the youngest country in the world, on the surface, in our eyes, everything is active. However, exploring its inner workings makes one realize that for the sake of erotic pleasure, romantic life, and excessive material possessions, society is actually harboring the evils of corruption, and youth has decadent manifestations. These are shaking the foundations of urban civilization, are harming the will of youth, are hindering the soundness of the country, and are preventing the strength of the nation. It is indeed a huge potential crisis, a very serious situation where artists must quickly rise up, like rushing to the embankment to prevent a river, and do their best to exercise the mission of art. Thus, the sharp-eyed, intellectually rich, emotionally passionate, nationalistic artists in Hollywood, aware of the future collapse and today's dangerous situation, resolutely take on the responsibility that artists should have for the nation and the country, and exercise the mission of art in criticism. RKO Radio Pictures then produced "Spring Love," a film that benefits society and touches people's hearts.

A purposeful nation is truly admirable, constantly concentrating and dedicating itself to doing such preventative work, making the nation's walls as solid as iron. At the same time, it incessantly pays attention to and removes rust, and repairs the walls. In contrast, our Chinese nation's surroundings are surrounded by fences full of dog holes, and no one has ever paid attention to them. It truly makes people wring their hands and beat their chests, deeply lamenting their own people's lack of ambition. We have issued many, many calls for years, but the listeners all seem numb and indifferent, and even those with the title of artist are degenerating. How can this prevent the brutal Japanese from invading the Northeast? Ah, lack of ambition, lack of ambition.

"Spring Love," of course, cannot leave the issue of love like other films, but the transcendence of the theme makes people deeply admire it. The theme is about how an aspiring young man does not have no future just because he has no money in front of him, and only a young man who is rich but decadent has no place in the world. An old man owns wealth and has two daughters and a son. The son is decadent, indulging in wine, and the elder daughter is also decadent, becoming a wanderer. These are all harmed by money. The younger daughter meets a young man. Although the young man is not so poor that his family has no bread, his exhaustion in his career does make him inevitably expose his financial difficulties. However, his ambition cannot be bent, and he finds new joy in love, and the joy of the romantic period gives him a boost in his career. However, the sea of love always has storms, and it is really not easy to sail smoothly. Under the old man's machinations, a rift in love is seen, because the old man's younger daughter eventually finds him disposable. However, the young man will not despair. His plan actually touches the heart of the old man's eldest daughter, and she rises from decadence, looking forward to the journey of her career and moving forward with him. Only the unpromising younger brother remains decadent.

Why is the title called Holiday? Because the focus of the story is on New Year's Day.

Therefore, the corruption of society is criticized as much as possible, and the decadence of youth is attacked as much as possible.

The protagonist of the film is the renowned Ann Harding, and the supporting cast is also renowned, Mary Astor. Ann Harding plays the old man's eldest daughter, purely expressing the various stages of life of the character in her expressions: romance, decadence, melancholy, activity, and hope are all revealed in her expressions as much as possible. Coupled with her graceful figure, she becomes even more lovable and pitiful. Mary Astor is also not to be outdone, and her increased sensuality further enhances her beauty. In short, in addition to the theme that makes people appreciate this film, the two female stars make people feel a very strong interest.

No wonder its opening business in New York exceeded expectations.

Social News

The Political Organizations of Various Countries in the World by Mori Sen 184

Politics is the mechanism for maintaining social order. If political achievements are good, human life can be stable. If they are bad, human life falls into hardship. Therefore, the progress and development of society is also hindered, and it is impossible to know whether the country will be destroyed. From this, it can be seen that to make social order peaceful, there must be good political organizations. Those who want to study the world situation or social relations must be familiar with the political organizations of various countries. Over the years, the political organizations of various countries in the world have changed into various systems with the changes in history. The twentieth century is the central era of material civilization, science, and culture, and the way of politics is worthy of attention. Especially under the current situation in China, foreign troubles are pressing in, and domestic politics are still corrupt. Looking back at various countries in the world, they are changing their political organizations according to the environment, which is indeed enough to make us take it as a "stone from another mountain." So it becomes meaningful for me to introduce this book.

This book is compiled and translated by Mr. Liu Bomin, and it includes the political situation of more than 60 countries in the world, from the national system, political system, parliamentary system, electoral system, judicial organs, administrative organs to the local system, with detailed outlines, which can be used for general reference. This book not only describes the domestic political situation, but also includes the history of the establishment of the national system, so that readers can find clues from a causal relationship, unlike the direct narrative method of ordinary books. This book completely uses the method of warp and weft, explaining everything in a coherent manner, so that readers can read it consistently, not only understanding the domestic political organization of the country, but also understanding why the country is organized in such a way, and the relationship between various countries in the world.

Often when we see a change in the political system of a certain country in the newspaper, we only have a faint image in our minds and do not study further problems. In fact, the change in a country's political organization is not accidental, but inevitable. If we can understand its current political organization, then we will not suspect that future changes are out of the blue. Therefore, in the current era of economic recession and the rising tide of revolution, the authorities often cannot maintain the status quo, and the political organization is changing rapidly. Being able to spare a little time to look at the political organizations of various countries in the world is especially an urgent matter.

For example, in the recent Eastern Province incident, most Chinese people still do not understand who initiated this incident, or do not understand how Japan passed this kind of bill. This is really because they do not understand the political organization of Japan. Therefore, they may misunderstand that it was Nan Lu Xiang's arbitrary actions, or General Kanaya's plan. If you read this book, you can fully understand. The book provides a detailed analysis of Japan's political organization, such as the mutual relations and tasks of the Emperor, advisory bodies, Minister of the Interior, Privy Council, Cabinet, Weiyi Shangzou organs, and the National Assembly. It clearly states them separately, so that readers will not misunderstand that after seeing a certain abnormality in politics, it is just an accidental microbubble in the political tide, but can actually understand the origin, background, and trend of the situation.

This book is divided into seven sections. The first section is a general discussion of (1) human life and politics, (2) the historical changes of politics, and (3) the general situation of politics in various countries. It explains that in order to make politics good and life stable, everyone must be able to understand politics, and it says that because everyone hopes for good politics and stable life, frequent political changes have occurred. Next, it discusses the general situation of world politics. The author says, "We have examined the political process from the past, and how many failures have occurred, and how many unreasonable politics have been experienced. Now it seems that we have reached some progress in politics." He also says, "After the Great War in Europe, the number of republics increased to fourteen, which is more than the twelve monarchies. Now there are already thirty-nine republics in the world, accounting for more than 60% of the number of countries in the world. Looking back at the political situation a hundred or two hundred years ago, it cannot be said that there have been great changes." This kind of historical statistics shows the characteristics of this book, knowing how painstakingly the author hopes for "removing the old and creating the new." Therefore, in addition to giving readers an image, this book can also give readers excitement, to the point that they may not feel that he is describing it in a ledger style, but make people interested in reading it. The second section is Europe, the third section is Asia, the fourth section is North America, the fifth section is South America, the sixth section is Oceania, and the seventh section is Africa. Only China is missing, which is because the people of this country always know their own political organization. At the same time, it is also giving the people of this country an implication, because it allows us to see the good political organizations of other countries, and to reform the politics of our country. Recently, I heard that the political organization of our country is about to undergo some changes again. I hope that readers will read this book first, and then have some understanding of the politics of this country and make some contributions, which is really an urgent task at present.

After reading this book, you can fully understand the current state of the political organizations of various countries in the world, but what will they be like in the future? This is certainly what we are anxious to know. This book also includes some introductions, because his words are so correct and powerful, so I do not mind repeating them here. He said, "European countries, whether monarchies or republics, are countries with extremely complex social problems. That is, in politics, countries where significant manifestations have already occurred, the activity rate of their politics is dominated by the Socialist Party and parties related to the Socialist Party, which is a phenomenon showing that the popularization of politics is still in progress. Compared with the political situation in the early twentieth century, it has already been a radical change. The great purpose of politics is to implement social policies earlier than those who are aware of it, so as to avoid gradual realization today. Striving to complete social policies and stabilize the lives of the majority of the people is the most important and urgent task today..." Therefore, we know that the trend of politics is gradually moving towards his path of progress, but how should the politics of this country be improved is a matter worthy of research. I hope that readers can first read this book to know what the world's politics are like, and then go on to explore the improvement of this country's politics, which may be more profound and practical.
